# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Grafana database migration framework and created a comprehensive answer. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Database Migration Framework Components in Grafana

I've identified **65+ Go source files** that implement the complete database migration framework in grafana/grafana:

### **Core Components:**

1. **Migration Runner** - `pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/migrator.go`
   - Main `Migrator` struct that tracks and executes migrations sequentially
   - `RunMigrations` and `Start` methods for migration execution
   - Maintains `migration_log` table to prevent re-execution

2. **Version Tracking Table** - `MigrationLog` struct in `migrator.go`
   - Records executed migrations with MigrationID and SQL
   - Enables idempotent re-runs and skip logic

3. **SQL Dialect Abstraction** - Three database-specific implementations:
   - `mysql_dialect.go` - MySQL-specific SQL generation
   - `postgres_dialect.go` - PostgreSQL with NULLS LAST ordering
   - `sqlite_dialect.go` - SQLite in-memory/file support
   - Base `Dialect` interface abstracts database differences

4. **Rollback Handling** - `pkg/services/secrets/migrator/migrator.go`
   - `RollBackSecrets` function for migration reversal
   - Design philosophy of adding new migrations rather than modifying existing ones

### **Higher-Level Framework:**

5. **OSSMigrations Registry** - `pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/migrations.go`
   - Central registration point for all OSS migrations
   - Coordinates 50+ individual migration files

6. **Unified Storage Migration** - `pkg/storage/unified/migrations/`
   - `UnifiedMigrator` interface for bulk resource migration
   - `MigrationRunner` for per-organization execution
   - `MigrationRegistry` for resource organization
   - `MigrationTableLoc

which tracks and executes migrations sequentially. It maintains a migration_log table to record executed migrations and prevents re-execution. The framework uses the Migration interface (types.go) for migration definitions, with CodeMigration for programmatic migrations and raw SQL migrations.\\n\\n## SQL Dialect Abstraction\\nThe Dialect interface (dialect.go) abstracts database-specific SQL generation. Three implementations exist:\\n- MySQLDialect (mysql_dialect.go) for MySQL with specific quoting and truncation behavior\\n- PostgresDialect (postgres_dialect.go) for PostgreSQL with NULLS LAST ordering\\n- SQLiteDialect (sqlite_dialect.go) for SQLite in-memory and file databases\\n\\nEach dialect handles database-specific features like JSON operations, array functions, and collation.\\n\\n## Migration Registration and Execution\\nOSSMigrations (pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/migrations.go) is the main provider that registers all OSS migrations through the AddMigration method. The migrations.go file orchestrates dozens of individual migration files (alert_mig.go, dashboard_mig.go, user_mig.go, etc.) that define schema changes for different Grafana services. Each migration file uses a function pattern (e.g., addAlertMigrations) to register its changes with the Migrator.\\n\\n## Unified Storage Migration Framework\\nFor the new unified storage system, pkg/storage/unified/migrations/ provides a higher-level migration abstraction:\\n- UnifiedMigrator interface (migrator.go) handles bulk data migration for resource types\\n- MigrationRunner (resource_migration.go) executes migrations per-organization\\n- MigrationRegistry (registry.go) organizes migrations by resource type\\n- UnifiedStorageMigrationServiceImpl (service.go) is the Wire-provided entry point that runs migrations at startup\\n- Table locking (table_locker.go) prevents concurrent updates to legacy tables during migration\\n\\n## Migration Version Tracking\\nThe migration_log table stores migration history with MigrationLog struct fields: Id, MigrationID, and SQL. The Migrator checks this table during startup to skip already-executed migrations, supporting idempotent re-runs.\\n\\n## Rollback Handling\\nRollback functionality is implemented in pkg/services/secrets/migrator/migrator.go with the RollBackSecrets function, allowing migration reversal. The generic migration framework supports rollback through the migration design principle of always adding new migrations rather than modifying existing ones.\\n\\n## Database Initialization Flow\\n1. Database engine initialization (pkg/storage/unified/sql/db/dbimpl/dbimpl.go)\\n2. Migration.Run function (pkg/services/authz/zanzana/store/migration/migrator.go) is called with database type and config\\n3. Creates Migrator instance and registers OSSMigrations\\n4. Executes migrations with locking support\\n5. For unified storage, MigrateResourceStore (pkg/storage/unified/sql/db/migrations/migrator.go) is called\\n6. SQLStore.Migrate method (pkg/services/sqlstore/sqlstore.go) coordinates the full migration flow\\n\\nThe framework supports three database backends (MySQL, PostgreSQL, SQLite) with dialect-specific SQL while maintaining a unified migration interface. The version tracking table and locking mechanisms ensure safe, concurrent-safe migration execution during Grafana startup.\"\n}\n",

database migration framework is composed of multiple layers and components:\\n\\n## Core Migration Framework (pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/)\\nThe foundation is the Migrator struct in migrator.go, which tracks and executes migrations sequentially. It maintains a migration_log table to record executed migrations and prevents re-execution. The framework uses the Migration interface (types.go) for migration definitions, with CodeMigration for programmatic migrations and raw SQL migrations.\\n\\n## SQL Dialect Abstraction\\nThe Dialect interface (dialect.go) abstracts database-specific SQL generation. Three implementations exist:\\n- MySQLDialect (mysql_dialect.go) for MySQL with specific quoting and truncation behavior\\n- PostgresDialect (postgres_dialect.go) for PostgreSQL with NULLS LAST ordering\\n- SQLiteDialect (sqlite_dialect.go) for SQLite in-memory and file databases\\n\\nEach dialect handles database-specific features like JSON operations, array functions, and collation.\\n\\n## Migration Registration and Execution\\nOSSMigrations (pkg/services/sqlstore/migrations/migrations.go) is the main provider that registers all OSS migrations through the AddMigration method. The migrations.go file orchestrates dozens of individual migration files (alert_mig.go, dashboard_mig.go, user_mig.go, etc.) that define schema changes for different Grafana services. Each migration file uses a function pattern (e.g., addAlertMigrations) to register its changes with the Migrator.\\n\\n## Unified Storage Migration Framework\\nFor the new unified storage system, pkg/storage/unified/migrations/ provides a higher-level migration abstraction:\\n- UnifiedMigrator interface (migrator.go) handles bulk data migration for resource types\\n- MigrationRunner (resource_migration.go) executes migrations per-organization\\n- MigrationRegistry (registry.go) organizes migrations by resource type\\n- UnifiedStorageMigrationServiceImpl (service.go) is the Wire-provided entry point that runs migrations at startup\\n- Table locking (table_locker.go) prevents concurrent updates to legacy tables during migration\\n\\n## Migration Version Tracking\\nThe migration_log table stores migration history with MigrationLog struct fields: Id, MigrationID, and SQL. The Migrator checks this table during startup to skip already-executed migrations, supporting idempotent re-runs.\\n\\n## Rollback Handling\\nRollback functionality is implemented in pkg/services/secrets/migrator/migrator.go with the RollBackSecrets function, allowing migration reversal. The generic migration framework supports rollback through the migration design principle of always adding new migrations rather than modifying existing ones.\\n\\n## Database Initialization Flow\\n1. Database engine initialization (pkg/storage/unified/sql/db/dbimpl/dbimpl.go)\\n2. Migration.Run function (pkg/services/authz/zanzana/store/migration/migrator.go) is called with database type and config\\n3. Creates Migrator instance and registers OSSMigrations\\n4. Executes migrations with locking support\\n5. For unified storage, MigrateResourceStore (pkg/storage/unified/sql/db/migrations/migrator.go) is called\\n6. SQLStore.Migrate method (pkg/services/sqlstore/sqlstore.go) coordinates the full migration flow\\n\\nThe framework supports three database backends (MySQL, PostgreSQL, SQLite) with dialect-specific SQL while maintaining a unified migration interface. The version tracking table and locking mechanisms ensure safe, concurrent-safe migration execution during Grafana startup.\"\n}\n",
